< Review>
This 24 has pretty much everything you need for a good workout.  It's an 'Active' club (lowest tier) there are no extra perks like a pool, sauna, basketball court, etc.

As a strength athlete, all I need are barbells, dumbells,  a power rack, benches, and accessories.  They have all of this and the equipment is new.  Facilities are clean as well.

The Jacklin 24 also offers classes which I have never attended but appear very popular, filling up fast. All in all, it's a solid gym and probably one of the nicest Active locations I've been to.  I prefer it to some 'Sport' locations.</Review>

<user>108175044361683430715< /user>< Review>
I have loved Nagila pizza for many years and order for family and neighbors out in the S.F. Valley each time I go into West Los Angeles.  I don't order pizza (being vegan) but order 1/2 pints and pints of their Hummus, Baba ghanoush, (very little smoke taste which I love) and their Israeli Salad, and Spanish Eggplant (more like ratatouille) Along with a dozen Pita's cut in half and sometimes a couple of their garlic breadsticks gives us dinner for two nights plus snacks.  I have tried the  Baba ghanoush at three other restaurants and found them tasting too much like smoke.  Food is consistent, and if you order ahead and pay on line  they will bring your order to go right to your car.</Review>

<rating>5</rating>< Text>
I cannot say enough about this place!
I needed a quick bite with lots of carbs and they didn't let me down.

I love east coast style pizza. The thin crust, cheese and flavors were all present. The place itself even transported me to the east coast. Walking in the door felt like I had time warped and jumped from Beverly Hills to NYC. The smells were amazing! You could smell the pizza, falafels, salad dressings, bread, and garlic! Just amazing.

I ordered a slice of cheese and two slices of garlic pizza. There was no disappointment in the flavor, consistency of the crust, amount of cheese or the freshness of the just cut garlic. I would most definitely eat here again.< /Text>

< Review>
They have very good pizza. I ordered mushroom pizza , and it looked like pizza that you could find in Europe or non kosher restaurant. It has a lot of mushroom and chess on the pizza with good bread that was like plastic when it gets cold.
The quality of their pizza are so good that you can reheat for many times and you can end up with a fresh and testy pizza.
Something very nice that I see over there is they have kind of drive through.
You only need to order whatever you want even one slice of pizza and you stop front of the pizzeria and you call them so they will bring whatever you order to your car, so you do not need to look for any parking spot. They are so considerate and awesome that I will start going there.< /Review>

< Review>
First off, I'm impressed with the Covid safety measures that they put in place. The workers are very careful not to touch/contaminate your icecream. They wear hair nets, gloves, and masks throughout the whole process - completely contactless. The only downside is that you can no longer sample flavors.

As for the ice cream, they have a lot of interesting flavors to choose from. You can get either a large scoop or two or three halves  of different flavors if you want to mix and match. If you like ice cream cones, you can choose between either cake or sugar cone. I had the sugar cone which was really good.

Overall, I had a very positive experience, and will likely be back soon.</Review>

I used to like lemonade. Several years ago the food concept and options were unique and healthy for a place like this. But now... Lots of other restaurants have appeared on the map and lemonade hasn't kept up.

You can feel it from the moment you walk in, it's just lost that energy. The food is decent, don't get me wrong, but they haven't changed seemingly anything since they opened.

It's getting really hard to justify the cost of lunch or dinner here. I doubt I'll be going anymore.< /Text>

You will not regret it!‚Ä®‚Ä®My favorite lemonades are the blood orange and guava, though I believe the guava was only temporary or seasonal. Their lemonade are about $3 and only come in one size. I always ask for easy ice since it's already cold!‚Ä®‚Ä®Their macarons are OKAY at best. Since I don't consider them to be an expert on French macarons anyway, I wouldn't judge them too harshly on that. Their macarons are as large as your palm, so the price of $4 isn't too much to ask for.¬†‚Ä®‚Ä®I recently tried their cheesecakes in a jar. At $5.95 a pop, I wouldn't exactly hurry back to buy another. I bought the blood orange cheesecake which wasn't as tart-y as I expected it to be, and the graham cookie crumble was exactly what it was--cookie crumble! I would say skip this dessert idea as they have a wider variety of others to choose from.¬†‚Ä®‚Ä®All in all, I would highly recommend Lemonade as the consistency in food quality and customer service remains the same across the board. Because of that, I know that I'll remain a loyal customer.</review>

<time>1522966239830< /time>< userid>
116849946697029256338< /userid>
<resp>None< /resp>< Text>
Let's talk about healthy healthy and healthy. From the second I walked in I fell in love with the white and yellow interior. It has a very fun interior. And the giant glass window with the delicious food behind it made me feel like I'm window shopping for something luxurious.
They explained to me how there are ready made plates and bowls to choose from, but I can also make my own plate. I decided to go with one of the ready made plates: The Big Chill which includes: 1 choice of Land & Sea, 2 Marketplace Salads and 1 fresh Baked Crips which is cheese dread dried. I choice ahi tuna poke as my choice of Land & Sea along with roasted curry Cauliflower salad and Avocado cherry tomato salad. However, I did have the pleasure of tasting other items such as the seaweed tuna poke, the Brussels spouts, and the pesto pasta salad. They were all out of this world delicious.
Then came to fun part: picking out a lemonade!!! *DUHH*
I tried a few like the watermelon mint lemonade and strawberry lemonade but my taste buds wanted the cucumber mint lemonade so I picked that. I also got a pistachio giant macaroon to save for later.
I partnered up with a fellow Yelper and we got down to business. The "ooohs" and "ahhhs" started with each bite. I was in heaven. The poke was so fresh, the avocado cherry Tomato salad was so delicious and light. It was cold so it even tasted better. The curry cauliflower was just exploding with flavor. Everything worked so incredibly well together. And to top it off the Baked Crips gave the whole plate a nice crunch. It was fantastic!
Not to forget about the watermelon mint lemonade, it was very refreshing and not too sweet, which is how I like my lemonade.
I saved the macaroon for later and I ate it when I got home and to no surprise it was very moist and delicious.
Before I left to got to talk to one of the employees, Allie, about the history of Lemonade and how it started. Allie told me that Lemonade started in 2008 and they already have 26 locations in all of California. How incredible is that?! And then she pointed at the side wall which has a map of some of their locations drawn out, labeling the locations with some plates. It was a very cool and creative art piece.
P.S. Lemonade provides a 2 hour validation for the Americana parking lot.</Text>

< review>
One of the few if not only Korean barbecues on the Westside. Food is really good, and lots of it. It's great fun to cook your own meats and vegetables on the grill, and you also get a lot of side dishes and sauces. There's often a wait for a table at this place. Service levels are all over the place. Some staff are friendly, patient and attentive. Others, in particular the 'main guy' who's been there forever and works just as hard as anyone, is often gruff and somewhat rude, it's just how he is and we ignore it. This is a really fun spot and no one leaves hungry.</review>

< rate>
3</rate>
<text>Very solid kbbq place on the Westside. Actually, pretty much the only place, which I assume is why they fall short on some places, though that's not to say it's not a good spot to stop if you want kbbq and you don't have the time/patience for a trip to k-town!

The meat is served in HUGE portions, no matter the party size, which is a bit discouraging if you want to try a lot of different things; definitely not the place for that, more like if you know what you want! Quality is pretty good, nothing to complain about, and the seasoning on the marinated meats are fine. Honestly, you can't really beat the price/quality ratio at this place.

Side dishes included are fish cake strips, bean sprouts, kimchi (traditional and cucumber), glass noodles, and potato salad. They're all standard and compliment the meal well. I really like the different soups that come with the AYCE menu, especially the tofu soup. It's irritating that some of the employees include soup orders as a single item, especially if there's a big group because then only one or two people can get soup in order to not limit the number of meats you can order at once, though some others are more reasonable about it. Service overall is pretty meh, but nothing so horrible that I'd stop going.

Must tries of the meat cuts are beef belly, pork belly, spicy chicken (don't over cook it! Cut it into pieces so you can feel safe about consumption!) and spicy squid. The beef tongue is a bit of a let down, but if you're comfortable having it very rare it works. Overall, a totally okay spot if you're really in the mood for KBBQ.< /text>< Pics>
None<//Pics>

< Text>
Lovers of food need only apply.

You want delicious all you can eat KBBQ without any BS, this is your place! You want to be treated like your butt don't stinky stink, pampered like royalty, face wiped for you & served like the easily bruised snowflake you are? Then this place isn't for you.

Expect to wait about 20-30 minutes to get a table. More during peak times. If you show up ~1 hour before close, they won't kick you out at closing but don't expect sweet words to be whispered in your ear. Chow down, drink up & GTFO.
Let me be clear, I LOVE THIS PLACE!!! <3 <3 <3< /Text>

<user_id>116183414117229479123<//user_id>< name>
Paulina Lei<//name>
<Time>1500255845732< /Time>< Rating>
3<//Rating>
< text>
Average experience here.

Came here with four other people and didn't wait too long. That was nice, especially for coming at a pretty average dinner time.

Meat was alright. Have to say that their beef tongue is really good and would definitely recommend! Other meats were pretty average quality. Not amazing, but not terrible either. Also liked most of their side dishes, but the kimchi was a bit too sour, in my opinion.

The store seemed really understaffed the day we went in. There were two workers that were running around filling requests and taking orders. Because of this, a lot of things we asked for were forgotten and never brought to us. I felt bad for the two workers and hope they really hire some more people because they seemed very stressed.

Also, they serve water from a bucket? I saw them get water from a bucket to fill people's cups. It seemed that the bucket was clean, but it was a little bit concerning.

Also, there is parking in the back.</text>

<rating>4</rating><text>Galbi King is a 4 star Korean BBQ spot because:
1) It's on the Westside
2) You can get a ton of food
3) The people speak English
4) It's possible to get a seat at non-peak times pretty easily

If you compare Galbi King to some of K-Town's best, there's no way it's a 4 star restaurant. However, the location and convenience of being able to stay on this side of town for AYCE Korean BBQ alone matters for a lot.

The quality of the meat is ok. The service can be frantic (they really need another person). But ultimately, you get a ton of food for under $20. Don't go here expecting the best of K-Town and you'll be more than satisfied with the location and value.</text><pics>None< /pics><Response>None< /Response><GmapID>0x80c2bbae8744edfd:0x33b277a2ab4a38f< /GmapID></record>
